  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ab178656-c318-4035-9d9d-02f1619917a1'
      });
    }

      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3556502945" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7865056822486241078">One of my all time favorite poems of all time. A gorgeous love story darkened by loss and disapproving fathers. <br/><br/>I’m lucky enough to live near Charleston, and have visited the graveyard where Annabel Lee is buried several times. For those who may not know the local lore, she was from a fairly prominent Charleston family. Her father did not approve of her being with Poe, as writers at that time were basically considered no better than unemployed, not to mention his penchant for alcohol. Poe had to</span>
  <span id="freeText7865056822486241078" style="display:none">One of my all time favorite poems of all time. A gorgeous love story darkened by loss and disapproving fathers. <br /><br />I’m lucky enough to live near Charleston, and have visited the graveyard where Annabel Lee is buried several times. For those who may not know the local lore, she was from a fairly prominent Charleston family. Her father did not approve of her being with Poe, as writers at that time were basically considered no better than unemployed, not to mention his penchant for alcohol. Poe had to travel at one point and while he was away, Annabel was struck with an illness that took her young life. When she was buried, her father was so spiteful with hatred towards Poe that he didn’t want Poe to be able to visit her gravesite and properly say his goodbyes and mourn, so he paid for six elaborate large stones, unmarked, placed in the graveyard, and to this day, no one knows which one she truly is buried under. </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1749145531?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/7365405-james">James</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7365405-james?shelf=1-fiction">1-fiction</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1749145531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6269914412185700842"><b>
  <i>
    <u>Book Review</u>
  </i>
</b><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe' title='Edgar Allan Poe' rel='nofollow noopener'>Edgar Allan Poe</a> is one of my three favorite poets and short story writers. In this poem, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/178911.Annabel_Lee' title='Annabel Lee by Edgar Allan Poe' rel='nofollow noopener'>Annabel Lee</a>, Poe pontificates on the love between two people, which suffers upon the death of one. Love is powerful. Love can also be dark. All that you'd expect from the mysterious suspense is firmly planted in this poem, but under a romantic guise; it's different than his other works, but you can still tell it was written by him. Published in the 1849, it may be his most haunting poe</span>
  <span id="freeText6269914412185700842" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <u>Book Review</u>
  </i>
</b><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe" rel="nofollow noopener">Edgar Allan Poe</a> is one of my three favorite poets and short story writers. In this poem, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/178911.Annabel_Lee" title="Annabel Lee by Edgar Allan Poe" rel="nofollow noopener">Annabel Lee</a>, Poe pontificates on the love between two people, which suffers upon the death of one. Love is powerful. Love can also be dark. All that you'd expect from the mysterious suspense is firmly planted in this poem, but under a romantic guise; it's different than his other works, but you can still tell it was written by him. Published in the 1849, it may be his most haunting poem; it was also released just around his death. He passed away at 40 years old, young even for 175 years ago. Many think the poem is about his relationship with his own young wife. I couldn't say. All I know is that rhyme and the staccato temperament in both the words and the timing is top notch. Roll the words off your lips, feel the energy, and absorb the pain. It's how to best understand Mr. Poe.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>About Me</u>
  </i>
</b><br />For those new to me or my reviews... here's the scoop: I read A LOT. I write A LOT. And now I blog A LOT. First the book review goes on Goodreads, and then I send it on over to my WordPress blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://thisismytruthnow.com">https://thisismytruthnow.com</a>, where you'll also find TV &amp; Film reviews, the revealing and introspective 365 Daily Challenge and lots of blogging about places I've visited all over the world. And you can find all my social media profiles to get the details on the who/what/when/where and my pictures. Leave a comment and let me know what you think. Vote in the poll and ratings. <div id="review_29958100" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29958100" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1182857-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506562769p2/1182857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29958100?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/1182857-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1182857-jennifer?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1182857-jennifer?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29958100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10875482279514963630">So exquisite and bittersweet is this poem, my comments don't do it justice. I have included it below:<br/><br/><br/>It was many and many a year ago,<br/>In a kingdom by the sea,<br/>That a maiden there lived whom you may know<br/>By the name of ANNABEL LEE;<br/>And this maiden she lived with no other thought<br/>Than to love and be loved by me.<br/><br/>I was a child and she was a child,<br/>In this kingdom by the sea;<br/>But we loved with a love that was more than love-<br/>I and my Annabel Lee;<br/>With a love that the winged seraphs of heaven<br/>Coveted her and me</span>
  <span id="freeText10875482279514963630" style="display:none">So exquisite and bittersweet is this poem, my comments don't do it justice. I have included it below:<br /><br /><br />It was many and many a year ago,<br />In a kingdom by the sea,<br />That a maiden there lived whom you may know<br />By the name of ANNABEL LEE;<br />And this maiden she lived with no other thought<br />Than to love and be loved by me.<br /><br />I was a child and she was a child,<br />In this kingdom by the sea;<br />But we loved with a love that was more than love-<br />I and my Annabel Lee;<br />With a love that the winged seraphs of heaven<br />Coveted her and me.<br /><br />And this was the reason that, long ago,<br />In this kingdom by the sea,<br />A wind blew out of a cloud, chilling<br />My beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />So that her highborn kinsman came<br />And bore her away from me,<br />To shut her up in a sepulchre<br />In this kingdom by the sea.<br /><br />The angels, not half so happy in heaven,<br />Went envying her and me-<br />Yes!- that was the reason (as all men know,<br />In this kingdom by the sea)<br />That the wind came out of the cloud by night,<br />Chilling and killing my Annabel Lee.<br /><br />But our love it was stronger by far than the love<br />Of those who were older than we-<br />Of many far wiser than we-<br />And neither the angels in heaven above,<br />Nor the demons down under the sea,<br />Can ever dissever my soul from the soul<br />Of the beautiful Annabel Lee.<br /><br />For the moon never beams without bringing me dreams<br />Of the beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />And the stars never rise but I feel the bright eyes<br />Of the beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />And so, all the night-tide, I lie down by the side<br />Of my darling- my darling- my life and my bride,<br />In the sepulchre there by the sea,<br />In her tomb by the sounding sea. <br /></span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2192819266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16703931097070864066">Poe might tell you that this poem is like life...it starts out as a fairytale and deteriorates into a horror story. I see it primarily as an attempt to explain the intensity of love and how it can endure and conquer even the unconquerable. <br/><br/>First, there is the great awe of being loved, of being innocent and free. Annabel Lee is known and beloved by all, but she only loves him. You can sense his amazement in having her love, but at this point in the poem he is deserving of it, for he is innocent a</span>
  <span id="freeText16703931097070864066" style="display:none">Poe might tell you that this poem is like life...it starts out as a fairytale and deteriorates into a horror story. I see it primarily as an attempt to explain the intensity of love and how it can endure and conquer even the unconquerable. <br /><br />First, there is the great awe of being loved, of being innocent and free. Annabel Lee is known and beloved by all, but she only loves him. You can sense his amazement in having her love, but at this point in the poem he is deserving of it, for he is innocent as well:<br /><br /><i>I was a child and she was child, <br />In this kingdom by the sea: <br />But we loved with a love that was more than love--<br />I and my Annabel Lee;</i><br /><br />In myth, the jealousy of the gods is always destructive to humans, and Poe uses that device to account for his loss of his love. Of course, with her goes his innocence and the kingdom becomes a bleak and tormented place.<br /><br />While many focus on the bizarre and almost horrific image at the end of the poem, I think this is more about the transcendent power of love and death's inability to annihilate it. He is able to hold on to her in his mind and his dreams. If he lies down with her figuratively, he is winning over death; if he lies down with her literally, than death has won for he is mad. Either way, love has won, for it endures.<br /><br />I have read this poem so many times that I can almost quote it by rote. It never fails to awaken something in me, a kind of mood, a sort of longing; and it always makes me think of those whom I have loved and lost and who are never that far away from my heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16703931097070864066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_744439523" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/744439523" />
    <a title="Nicole~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20071931-nicole"><img alt="Nicole~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439784920p2/20071931.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/744439523?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole~" href="/user/show/20071931-nicole">Nicole~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer744439523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11094508051132326342">Inspired by the creepy season, I have been reading Edgar Allan Poe's biography by Jeffrey Meyers. One of the interesting tidbits that came up was that he married his first cousin, Virginia Clemm, when she was only 13 years old. Virginia was an attractive girl with a well rounded figure and the appearance of a more mature woman. She had a gentle nature and aspired to be a skilled musician and singer.<br/>In a tearful letter to his Aunt Maria, Virginia's mother, Poe swore his fervent devotion to Virgin</span>
  <span id="freeText11094508051132326342" style="display:none">Inspired by the creepy season, I have been reading Edgar Allan Poe's biography by Jeffrey Meyers. One of the interesting tidbits that came up was that he married his first cousin, Virginia Clemm, when she was only 13 years old. Virginia was an attractive girl with a well rounded figure and the appearance of a more mature woman. She had a gentle nature and aspired to be a skilled musician and singer.<br>In a tearful letter to his Aunt Maria, Virginia's mother, Poe swore his fervent devotion to Virginia, so tormented was he that she might leave him. After secretly marrying in September 1935, Poe, then 27 years old, publicly married Virginia on May 16th, 1836; she had not quite reached her 14th year. Poe declared passionately that he loved Virginia, although throughout his married years he did not appear that ardent. Virginia was said to have loved Poe first as a brother or cousin, but eventually grew to love him as a husband and lover.<br>Sadly, in 1847, Virginia died at the very young age of 25 years from Tuberculosis, the same illness that robbed Poe of his mother, Eliza Poe. Poe was devastated. The impact of the deaths of his loved ones by the same disease are clearly reflected in his poems. While <u>The Raven</u> might illuminate Poe's constant fear of the "messenger of death", <u>Ulalume</u> and <u>Annabel Lee</u> were undoubtedly inspired by Virginia's life. In May 1849, he completed the latter, and although many of Poe's other lady loves had claimed it was, in part, about them, <i>Annabel Lee</i> referenced in the lines, " she was a child," and " my life and my bride" undeniably would have been Virginia. <br>The seemingly fairytale quality would suggest that it was a loving tribute to the gentle, fragile Virginia, however inadequate a consolation to his broken heart.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382194560i/5745965._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo image_zpsd4fc1802.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11094508051132326342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1953750229" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1953750229" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1953750229?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=picturebooks">picturebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1953750229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9735775611636679860">The poem by Edgar Allan Poe set, by the artist, Gilles Tibo, in the 1930s on the Gaspé Peninsula, Quebec. I reread this because I am reading all these gothic texts for a class on madness, and we had already read “The Fall of the House of Usher.” So this is a gothic romantic text. Obsessive, all-encompassing love. There’s some question about what “the wind” might be that takes her life. And it’s not so much death that she experiences as she is “shut her up in a sepulchre,” as if they were eternal</span>
  <span id="freeText9735775611636679860" style="display:none">The poem by Edgar Allan Poe set, by the artist, Gilles Tibo, in the 1930s on the Gaspé Peninsula, Quebec. I reread this because I am reading all these gothic texts for a class on madness, and we had already read “The Fall of the House of Usher.” So this is a gothic romantic text. Obsessive, all-encompassing love. There’s some question about what “the wind” might be that takes her life. And it’s not so much death that she experiences as she is “shut her up in a sepulchre,” as if they were eternally together in spite of the death. Or buried alive! There’s that notion that the angels, “her highborn kingsmen,” killed her so they could have her instead of him. But then he never gets over her loss, Ever. The “sepulchre” is here conceived as a pale ghost ship by Tibo, whose playful, then ethereal, art is lovely. A classic gothic text about eternal love and grief.<br /><br />Annabel Lee<br /><br />It was many and many a year ago,<br />In a kingdom by the sea,<br />That a maiden there lived whom you may know<br />By the name of ANNABEL LEE;<br />And this maiden she lived with no other thought<br />Than to love and be loved by me.<br /><br />I was a child and she was a child,<br />In this kingdom by the sea;<br />But we loved with a love that was more than love-<br />I and my Annabel Lee;<br />With a love that the winged seraphs of heaven<br />Coveted her and me.<br /><br />And this was the reason that, long ago,<br />In this kingdom by the sea,<br />A wind blew out of a cloud, chilling<br />My beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />So that her highborn kinsman came<br />And bore her away from me,<br />To shut her up in a sepulchre<br />In this kingdom by the sea.<br /><br />The angels, not half so happy in heaven,<br />Went envying her and me-<br />Yes!- that was the reason (as all men know,<br />In this kingdom by the sea)<br />That the wind came out of the cloud by night,<br />Chilling and killing my Annabel Lee.<br /><br />But our love it was stronger by far than the love<br />Of those who were older than we-<br />Of many far wiser than we-<br />And neither the angels in heaven above,<br />Nor the demons down under the sea,<br />Can ever dissever my soul from the soul<br />Of the beautiful Annabel Lee.<br /><br />For the moon never beams without bringing me dreams<br />Of the beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />And the stars never rise but I feel the bright eyes<br />Of the beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />And so, all the night-tide, I lie down by the side<br />Of my darling- my darling- my life and my bride,<br />In the sepulchre there by the sea,<br />In her tomb by the sounding sea. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9735775611636679860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13614320890863249730" style="display:none"><i>It was many and many a year ago, <br /> In a kingdom by the sea, <br />That a maiden there lived whom you may know <br /> By the name of Annabel Lee; <div id="review_3442654681" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3442654681" />
    <a title="KIKI" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/94645972-kiki"><img alt="KIKI" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598342946p2/94645972.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3442654681?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KIKI" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KIKI" href="/user/show/94645972-kiki">KIKI</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/39404257-annabelle-lee">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/94645972-kiki?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3442654681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8981446666356444033">5 STARS!<br/><br/><br/><b><i>I </i>was a child and <i>she </i>was a child,<br/>   In this kingdom by the sea:<br/>But we loved with a love that was more than love—<br/>   I and my Annabel Lee;<br/>With a love that the winged seraphs of heaven<br/>   Coveted her and me.<br/><br/><br/></b>The first time I read <i>Annabel Lee</i>, I was reading Lady Midnight by Cassandra Clare. It’s heavily featured in the book and the chapter titles are named after lines from the poem. In The Dark Artifices series, Edgar Allan Poe heard of a tragic story from Downworlders and was inspired to wri</span>
  <span id="freeText8981446666356444033" style="display:none">5 STARS!<br /><br /><br /><b><i>I </i>was a child and <i>she </i>was a child,<br />   In this kingdom by the sea:<br />But we loved with a love that was more than love—<br />   I and my Annabel Lee;<br />With a love that the winged seraphs of heaven<br />   Coveted her and me.<br /><br /><br /></b>The first time I read <i>Annabel Lee</i>, I was reading Lady Midnight by Cassandra Clare. It’s heavily featured in the book and the chapter titles are named after lines from the poem. In The Dark Artifices series, Edgar Allan Poe heard of a tragic story from Downworlders and was inspired to write this poem shortly before his death. The story is about the Shadowhunter Annabel Blackthorn and her warlock lover Malcolm Fade. Annabel Lee describes the story of two people who fell in love in their youth, told in a way that the narrator is the lover of Annabel Lee. Though they were young, they shared a love so strong that the angels apparently grew envious, and her highborn kinsmen took her away before she was eventually killed by what her lover believes to be the angels. She is buried in a tomb by the sea, and the narrator, believing their souls entwined, refuses to let death keep them apart, and spends his nights lying by her tomb, dreaming of Annabel and seeing her in the stars.<br /><br /><i>Annabel Lee </i>will always hold a place in my heart. It’s always been such a meaningful poem to me and I think it’s one of Poe’s best work. He wrote this poem after the death of his beloved wife Virginia. His tone and mood demonstrate that of content and acceptance of the death of his wife, yet remembering of their love and the fact that no one could “ever dissever my soul from the soul of the beautiful Annabel Lee...” A perfect rendition of a very sad thought and symbolic of the writing of Poe, depicting sadness to the core with intricacies of life and reality as experienced. A soulful expression of a loss. A beautiful last work of the great Edgar Allan Poe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8981446666356444033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15169590737062201149" style="display:none">I don't read poems and this was my first, probably because one of my favourite series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/76298-the-dark-artifices" rel="nofollow noopener">The dark Artifices </a> by Cassandra Clare has quotes form this poem in it and I enjoyed that book so very much! <div id="review_1254092012" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1254092012" />
    <a title="Joanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39412583-joanna"><img alt="Joanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422469285p2/39412583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1254092012?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanna" href="/user/show/39412583-joanna">Joanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1254092012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8356417220893445060">In high school, I remember having to read about Edgar Allen Poe and my teacher would repeat how dark his life was. Learning about things Poe went through and then reading some of his poetry can help you understand his way of writing. This poem, Annabel Lee, is beautiful in the way he describes his love towards her, and at the same time sad because of her death. <br/>In this poem, Poe is describing how strong their love was. They both were so in love that their love was greater than anything and anyon</span>
  <span id="freeText8356417220893445060" style="display:none">In high school, I remember having to read about Edgar Allen Poe and my teacher would repeat how dark his life was. Learning about things Poe went through and then reading some of his poetry can help you understand his way of writing. This poem, Annabel Lee, is beautiful in the way he describes his love towards her, and at the same time sad because of her death. <br />In this poem, Poe is describing how strong their love was. They both were so in love that their love was greater than anything and anyone else. They were so young, yet he describes their love as something more than just a simple feeling. Their bonding was too strong that death decided to tear them apart. She died and he blames it on life for envying their love and taking her away from him, but death doesn’t stop their souls from wanting each other.<br />I like every line of this Poem, from the beginning to the end. The beginning is all flowers and butterflies, Poe describes their love for each other as if they were the perfect match and loved one another to their fullest. “The angels went envying her and me… Yes! – that was the reason… That the wind came out of the cloud by night, Chilling and killing my Annabel Lee,” I believe what Poe was trying to say here is that now that he had happiness life, couldn’t accept it and took that happiness away from him. The ending sounds as if Poe was in love and he won’t love anyone else but her, but it could be argued he was on denial and going insane for how life has treated him.<br />The fact that this poem was made for his lover, makes the poem more alive. The expression and how Poe says why life took her away from him can actually be felt by the reader, in my opinion. Their love was so strong he could never stop thinking about her and as a matter of fact, it drove him insane in real life. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8356417220893445060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7304600461985075285">Uno de los más bellos poemas de amor y muerte. Disfrutadlo.<br/><br/><br/>Versión original de Edgar Allan Poe (1849):<br/><br/><br/>It was many and many a year ago,<br/> In a kingdom by the sea,<br/>That a maiden there lived whom you may know<br/> By the name of Annabel Lee;<br/>And this maiden she lived with no other thought<br/> Than to love and be loved by me.<br/>I was a child and she was a child,<br/> In this kingdom by the sea,<br/>But we loved with a love that was more than love—<br/> I and my Annabel Lee—<br/>With a love that the wingèd seraphs of Heaven<br/> Coveted her</span>
  <span id="freeText7304600461985075285" style="display:none">Uno de los más bellos poemas de amor y muerte. Disfrutadlo.<br /><br /><br />Versión original de Edgar Allan Poe (1849):<br /><br /><br />It was many and many a year ago,<br /> In a kingdom by the sea,<br />That a maiden there lived whom you may know<br /> By the name of Annabel Lee;<br />And this maiden she lived with no other thought<br /> Than to love and be loved by me.<br />I was a child and she was a child,<br /> In this kingdom by the sea,<br />But we loved with a love that was more than love—<br /> I and my Annabel Lee—<br />With a love that the wingèd seraphs of Heaven<br /> Coveted her and me.<br />And this was the reason that, long ago,<br /> In this kingdom by the sea,<br />A wind blew out of a cloud, chilling<br /> My beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />So that her highborn kinsmen came<br /> And bore her away from me,<br />To shut her up in a sepulchre<br /> In this kingdom by the sea.<br />The angels, not half so happy in Heaven,<br /> Went envying her and me—<br />Yes!—that was the reason (as all men know,<br /> In this kingdom by the sea)<br />That the wind came out of the cloud by night,<br /> Chilling and killing my Annabel Lee.<br />But our love it was stronger by far than the love<br /> Of those who were older than we—<br /> Of many far wiser than we—<br />And neither the angels in Heaven above<br /> Nor the demons down under the sea<br />Can ever dissever my soul from the soul<br /> Of the beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />For the moon never beams, without bringing me dreams<br /> Of the beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />And the stars never rise, but I feel the bright eyes<br /> Of the beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />And so, all the night-tide, I lie down by the side<br /> Of my darling—my darling—my life and my bride,<br /> In her sepulchre there by the sea—<br /> In her tomb by the sounding sea<br /><br /><br />Versión de Leopoldo María Panero (publicado en de Poesía. 1970-1985; Visor, 1986): <br /><br />Hay un nombre cuyo ruido hace<br />temblar al aire como si fuera de algo<br />el de mi hermosa ANNABEL LEE: el de una niña<br />que me amó como si yo algo fuera<br />y que al morir supo tan sólo<br />a Dios decir un nombre, un ruido:<br /><br />ANNABEL LEE.<br /><br />Yo era una niña y ella casi un niño<br />nadando los dos bajo el mar; pero<br />nos amábamos ambos de algo como hierro<br />y llorábamos juntos los dos, bajo el cielo.<br />Y fue ese el motivo quizá por el que un día<br />una lágrima cayó del cielo disolviendo<br />como un ácido el cuerpo que temblaba<br />de mi hermosa, de mi pálida ANNABEL LEE, y entonces<br />vinieron sus padres, gente de dinero<br />a hacerse cargo del alma, y dicen<br />que la enterraron bajo el mar.<br /><br />Pero hoy los huesos de una niña bailan<br />allí junto a una roca, cerca<br />de aquel reino moribundo que hay<br />debajo del mar, y cantan<br />aún esa canción demente, la<br />de los seres que<br />se enterraron juntos pronunciando<br />a solas el nombre de<br /><br />ANNABEL LEE.<br /><br /><br />Adaptación musicada de Radio Futura (1987):<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BuZMhbU5TPY">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BuZMh...</a><br /></span>

  <b>It was many and many a year ago,<br/>In a kingdom by the sea,<br/>That a maiden there lived whom you may know<br/>By the name of Annabel Lee;<br/>And this maiden she lived with no other thought<br/>Than to love and be loved by me.<br/><br/>I was a child and she was a child,<br/>In this kingdom by the sea;<br/>But we loved with a love that was more than love-<br/>I and my Annabel Lee;<br/>With a love that the winged seraphs of heaven<br/>Coveted her and me.</b>

<div id="review_1253499277" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1253499277" />
    <a title="Frank Corral" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29957143-frank-corral"><img alt="Frank Corral" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424322354p2/29957143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1253499277?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frank Corral" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frank Corral" href="/user/show/29957143-frank-corral">Frank Corral</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1253499277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6306826862354821869">"Annabel Lee" by the Prince of Literary Darkness <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe' title='Edgar Allan Poe' rel='nofollow noopener'> Edgar Allan Poe</a> is thought of as some of his "lighter work", however I disagree though Annabel Lee is not as morbid as some of his other writings it is just as dark and charming as we would expect from Mr. Poe. <br/>The Poem follows Poe's feelings towards his childhood love of a girl by the name of Annabel Lee, they live happily in a "Kingdom by the Sea" laughing and playing as kids do. Their love is so strong and they live so peacefully that even God</span>
  <span id="freeText6306826862354821869" style="display:none">"Annabel Lee" by the Prince of Literary Darkness <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe" rel="nofollow noopener"> Edgar Allan Poe</a> is thought of as some of his "lighter work", however I disagree though Annabel Lee is not as morbid as some of his other writings it is just as dark and charming as we would expect from Mr. Poe. <br />The Poem follows Poe's feelings towards his childhood love of a girl by the name of Annabel Lee, they live happily in a "Kingdom by the Sea" laughing and playing as kids do. Their love is so strong and they live so peacefully that even God's Angels in heaven are envious of him and find it necessary to take Annabel Lee from him, locked up in a Tomb or "Sepulchre".<br />Poe's writing is incredible, there are so many dark and twisted hidden messages in his writing, however one must dig much deeper in his writing and his personal life to truly understand these hidden messages. We understand that they are children living in a "kingdom" is it truly a kingdom probably not but if they are kids their innocence and imagination makes them feel like royalty, perhaps this is poe describing a young couple that feel life kids again, it is interesting how Poe married his first cousin Virginia Clemm when she was 13 and Poe was 27. Looking further into his life, he had many deaths that heavily affected his life, many of these deaths were family and loved ones. I believe that Poe admired the innocence of a child, perhaps looking back and remembering how everything was simpler back then.<br />Further into the Poem we understand that these "Angels" are envious of Poe and his love, I can see how bitter Poe is at this point. Hes angry, why wouldn't he be, he lost the only thing that made him happy, its unfair for these "higher beings" to hate him this much. Still even after death he will always remember his true love, this is down right beautiful, Poe is truly a master of the dark, the morbid, the twisted, and all these traits are here but "Annabel Lee" is a perfect example of Poes mastery of a true love story.<br />"And neither the angels in heaven above,<br />Nor the demons down under the sea,<br />Can ever dissever my soul from the soul<br />Of the beautiful Annabel Lee.<br />For the moon never beams without bringing me dreams<br />Of the beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />And the stars never rise but I feel the bright eyes<br />Of the beautiful Annabel Lee;<br />And so, all the night-tide, I lie down by the side<br />Of my darling- my darling- my life and my bride,<br />In the sepulchre there by the sea,<br />In her tomb by the sounding sea."</span>
  <a data-text-id="6306826862354821869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1211873687" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1211873687" />
    <a title="Cee (The Mistress Case)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37784247-cee-the-mistress-case"><img alt="Cee (The Mistress Case)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475961354p2/37784247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1211873687?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cee (The Mistress Case)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cee (The Mistress Case)" href="/user/show/37784247-cee-the-mistress-case">Cee (The Mistress Case)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24245914-annabel-lee">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37784247-cee-the-mistress-case?shelf=ultimate-favorite-cases">ultimate-favorite-cases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37784247-cee-the-mistress-case?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1211873687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16773875036586419966">My favorite of Edgar Allan Poe's stories! My favorite poem ever, actually.<br/><br/>Many people consider <i>Annabel Lee</i> the "lightest" of Edgar Allan Poe's work and define it as a bittersweet poem. However, I find it downright bitter, sorrowful, and unforgiving and I guess that all depends on one's perception and interpretation. Reminiscing can only torture a broken heart for so long.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427085921ra/14179682.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>"It was many and many a year ago,<br/>In a kingdom by the sea,<br/>That a maiden there lived whom you may know<br/>By the name of Annabel Lee</span>
  <span id="freeText16773875036586419966" style="display:none">My favorite of Edgar Allan Poe's stories! My favorite poem ever, actually.<br><br>Many people consider <i>Annabel Lee</i> the "lightest" of Edgar Allan Poe's work and define it as a bittersweet poem. However, I find it downright bitter, sorrowful, and unforgiving and I guess that all depends on one's perception and interpretation. Reminiscing can only torture a broken heart for so long.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427085921ra/14179682.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>"It was many and many a year ago,<br>In a kingdom by the sea,<br>That a maiden there lived whom you may know<br>By the name of Annabel Lee;<br>And this maiden she lived with no other thought<br>Than to love and be loved by me.<br><br>I was a child and she was a child,<br>In this kingdom by the sea;<br>But we loved with a love that was more than love-<br>I and my Annabel Lee;<br>With a love that the winged seraphs of heaven<br>Coveted her and me.<br><br>And this was the reason that, long ago,<br>In this kingdom by the sea,<br>A wind blew out of a cloud, chilling<br>My beautiful Annabel Lee;<br>So that her highborn kinsman came<br>And bore her away from me,<br>To shut her up in a sepulchre<br>In this kingdom by the sea.<br><br>The angels, not half so happy in heaven,<br>Went envying her and me-<br>Yes!- that was the reason (as all men know,<br>In this kingdom by the sea)<br>That the wind came out of the cloud by night,<br>Chilling and killing my Annabel Lee.<br><br>But our love it was stronger by far than the love<br>Of those who were older than we-<br>Of many far wiser than we-<br>And neither the angels in heaven above,<br>Nor the demons down under the sea,<br>Can ever dissever my soul from the soul<br>Of the beautiful Annabel Lee.<br><br>For the moon never beams without bringing me dreams<br>Of the beautiful Annabel Lee;<br>And the stars never rise but I feel the bright eyes<br>Of the beautiful Annabel Lee;<br>And so, all the night-tide, I lie down by the side<br>Of my darling- my darling- my life and my bride,<br>In the sepulchre there by the sea,<br>In her tomb by the sounding sea."<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396706788ra/9174939.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16773875036586419966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_586930844" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/586930844" />
    <a title="Samantha Spilotro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12707017-samantha-spilotro"><img alt="Samantha Spilotro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365631300p2/12707017.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/586930844?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha Spilotro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha Spilotro" href="/user/show/12707017-samantha-spilotro">Samantha Spilotro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer586930844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16254545730267364656">"Annabel Lee" is a beautiful, but painfully sad poem. It talks about a young love between man and a beautiful maid named Annabel Lee. The angels envied the two lovers. The angels send a chilling wind that killed beautiful Annabel Lee. I would recommend this poem to anyone that loves and understand poetry. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2355014.Ozymandias"><img alt="Ozymandias" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1356208377l/2355014._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gqr89cmIiima0TIIuaM4TJ+ZK5MPW4pxHRX66/M2WTs7AfcMoF7IWYHzTPmEklMCbL+SD6uL+1kyRiCHr+TFhg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hFawu0KOsB48P8Ox6FE7/9BOHHkxqZIWEQex/GNZH749/btCK1jybicdvUDVYFCxI2il5ZV54z4+VGuQP4uDAw==')})
  }
//]]>

These beautiful images create a parallel story accessible to children: Lonely little Robot doesn\'t have much to be happy about, working all day in the factory. One day while sadly walking by himself, he follows a bird over a hill, where he finds a field of daffodils. After dancing with them, his spirit is filled with joy. Children will observe the contrast between the dreary, metallic robot world, and the lively, colorful world of the daffodils and nature. They will cheer little Robot for sharing the power of nature with the others, bringing happiness to the once dismal factory. In an effort to have children understand the basic themes of the poem, easily recognizable characters such as robots and animated flowers are used to act out the poetic verse. Bold illustrations and easy-to-read text lend themselves to lap-reading and group story time. Children will relate to the basic emotions (sadness, loneliness, happiness) of the robots, and can be encouraged to think about what cheers them up when they are sad, and to talk about how nature makes them feel.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe">About Edgar Allan Poe</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1454522972p3/4624490.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe">Edgar Allan Poe
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12954050684590480171">The name Poe brings to mind images of murderers and madmen, premature burials, and mysterious women who return from the dead. His works have been in print since 1827 and include such literary classics as <i>The Tell-Tale Heart</i>, <i>The Raven</i>, and The Fall of the House of Usher. This versatile writer’s oeuvre includes short stories, poetry, a novel, a textbook, a book of scientific theory, and hundreds of</span>
  <span id="freeText12954050684590480171" style="display:none">The name Poe brings to mind images of murderers and madmen, premature burials, and mysterious women who return from the dead. His works have been in print since 1827 and include such literary classics as <i>The Tell-Tale Heart</i>, <i>The Raven</i>, and The Fall of the House of Usher. This versatile writer’s oeuvre includes short stories, poetry, a novel, a textbook, a book of scientific theory, and hundreds of essays and book reviews. He is widely acknowledged as the inventor of the modern detective story and an innovator in the science fiction genre, but he made his living as America’s first great literary critic and theoretician. Poe’s reputation today rests primarily on his tales of terror as well as on his haunting lyric poetry.<br /><br />Just as the bizarre characters in Poe’s stories have captured the public imagination so too has Poe himself. He is seen as a morbid, mysterious figure lurking in the shadows of moonlit cemeteries or crumbling castles. This is the Poe of legend. But much of what we know about Poe is wrong, the product of a biography written by one of his enemies in an attempt to defame the author’s name.<br /><br />The real Poe was born to traveling actors in Boston on January 19, 1809. Edgar was the second of three children. His other brother William Henry Leonard Poe would also become a poet before his early death, and Poe’s sister Rosalie Poe would grow up to teach penmanship at a Richmond girls’ school. Within three years of Poe’s birth both of his parents had died, and he was taken in by the wealthy tobacco merchant John Allan and his wife Frances Valentine Allan in Richmond, Virginia while Poe’s siblings went to live with other families. Mr. Allan would rear Poe to be a businessman and a Virginia gentleman, but Poe had dreams of being a writer in emulation of his childhood hero the British poet Lord Byron. Early poetic verses found written in a young Poe’s handwriting on the backs of Allan’s ledger sheets reveal how little interest Poe had in the tobacco business.<br /><br />For more information, please see <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edgar_allan_poe">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edgar_al...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12954050684590480171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/trivia/work/1632052-annabel-lee">Trivia About Annabel Lee</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
        <div class="mediumText">
          2 trivia questions
